  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_41900833-f3d8-4581-a105-5ca6f9e4fe3f'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer6876200039820781686">Wicked wolves and a grim governess threaten Bonnie and her cousin Sylvia when Bonnie's parents leave Willoughby Chase for a sea voyage.   <span id="freeText6876200039820781686" style="display:none">Wicked wolves and a grim governess threaten Bonnie and her cousin Sylvia when Bonnie's parents leave Willoughby Chase for a sea voyage. Left in the care of the cruel Miss Slighcarp, the girls can hardly believe what is happening to their once happy home. The servants are dismissed, the furniture is sold, and Bonnie and Sylvia are sent to a prison-like orphan school. It seems as if the endless hours of drudgery will never cease.<br /><br />With the help of Simon the gooseboy and his flock, they escape. But how will they ever get Willoughby Chase free from the clutches of the evil Miss Slighcarp?</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1399451-are-the-other-books-in-the-series-needing">Are the other books in the series needing to be read in order? Also, are they as enthralling as the first?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1399451'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F36638.The_Wolves_of_Willoughby_Chase">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/32761625-cassandra"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1404450006i/32761625._UY100_CR3,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/32761625-cassandra">Cassandra</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The other books kinda need to be read in order, but you can read <i>Wolves</i> apart from them. The link is that #2, Black Hearts in Battersea, centres aroun<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The other books kinda need to be read in order, but you can read <i>Wolves</i> apart from them. The link is that #2, Black Hearts in Battersea, centres around Simon (side character in Wolves). The rest of the books are about Dido Twite, a side character from Black Hearts... hope that makes sense?<br /><br />The other books are good, but I didn't enjoy them as much because I really liked Bonnie and Sylvia and wanted to find out what happened to them.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2193629704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10013363762691816058">When Bonnie’s parents leave for a voyage across the sea, she’s left in the care of a strident governess: Miss Slighcarp. Soon joined by her cousin Sylvia, the girls suffer cruel treatment at the hands of their governess and watch as every joyful element of their lives is dismantled. Meanwhile, menacing wolves circle and a strange man joins in Miss Slighcarp’s machinations. If Bonnie & Sylvia are to be free and happy once more, they must turn to an odd boy and his flock of geese for help. <br/><br/>Aiken e</span>
  <span id="freeText10013363762691816058" style="display:none">When Bonnie’s parents leave for a voyage across the sea, she’s left in the care of a strident governess: Miss Slighcarp. Soon joined by her cousin Sylvia, the girls suffer cruel treatment at the hands of their governess and watch as every joyful element of their lives is dismantled. Meanwhile, menacing wolves circle and a strange man joins in Miss Slighcarp’s machinations. If Bonnie &amp; Sylvia are to be free and happy once more, they must turn to an odd boy and his flock of geese for help. <br /><br />Aiken evokes a marvelous sense of atmosphere, a sensation that’s heightened by the contrast between the outside world and the inside of Bonnie’s home: Willoughby Chase. A cold and haunting mood pervades the outside with its “<i>somber sighing of the wind and the hideous howling of the wolves</i>.” The hills are pleated with snow, icicles hang from the trees, and “<i>snow lay piled on the dark roads</i>.” <br /><br />Willoughby Chase is “<i>an inviting home – a warm and welcoming stronghold</i>.” Bonnie sleeps in a soft, warm bed, and she and Sylvia spend their afternoons in the nursery, which is “<i>gay with the sunshine that sparkled on crystal and silver and found golden light in the honey and quince preserves.</i>” <br /><br />Despite its alluring opening pages, <i>The Wolves of Willoughby Chase</i> unravels once its cookie-cutter characters step into the limelight. Intrigue vanishes as each character assumes a stereotypical role in the narrative. The only exception is, perhaps, Mr. Grimshaw who unexpectedly fires a “<i>long, heavy, glinting blue gun</i>” out of the train carriage he shares with young Sylvia, shooting at rabbits and ravens with a reckless air of perverse enjoyment. Mr. Grimshaw takes snuff and has no qualms about seizing a shard of glass and stabbing a wolf to death. <br /><br />Strangely, after a strong presence early in the narrative, the wolves fade into the background, eventually becoming a distant threat. However, <i>The Wolves of Willoughby Chase</i> is the first in a series of thirteen books, so perhaps their presence grows more prevalent over time. <br /><br />With such standard characters, the story inevitably arrives at a predictable conclusion.<br /><br /><i>The Wolves of Willoughby Chase</i> is a quick, enjoyable little read, but it’s nothing to write home about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10013363762691816058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2023484133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2023484133" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3144945-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594856152p2/3144945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2023484133?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/3144945-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2023484133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15039296655784070084">Those of us who grew up with an affinity for Victorian books, it might have started here, in Joan Aiken's 1962 classic Gothic / Dickensian love note, with its pitch perfect wicked governesses and wretched orphanages and aptronyms and moors and girls who are described as "hoydens," and secret passages, and real dungeons, and all these wolves. When we hit our teens and started reading stuff like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/713007711' title='My review of David Copperfield' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dickens</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154863435' title='My review' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wuthering Heights,</a> it felt familiar to us; we'd already been indoctrinated into the rules o</span>
  <span id="freeText15039296655784070084" style="display:none">Those of us who grew up with an affinity for Victorian books, it might have started here, in Joan Aiken's 1962 classic Gothic / Dickensian love note, with its pitch perfect wicked governesses and wretched orphanages and aptronyms and moors and girls who are described as "hoydens," and secret passages, and real dungeons, and all these wolves. When we hit our teens and started reading stuff like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/713007711" title="My review of David Copperfield" rel="nofollow noopener">Dickens</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154863435" title="My review" rel="nofollow noopener">Wuthering Heights,</a> it felt familiar to us; we'd already been indoctrinated into the rules of Victoria. <br /><br />It's set in an alternate history of England, where wolves are rampant and something about a King James III, who cares, how am I supposed to know whether a given King James is fictional or not, you can tell it's not the real world because this is a place where geese can be trusted. Geese cannot be trusted irl. They are wicked and they mean you harm.<br /><br />Here's <a href="http://blogs.slj.com/afuse8production/2012/05/24/top-100-childrens-novels-57-the-wolves-of-willoughby-chase-by-joan-aiken/" rel="nofollow noopener">a great piece on <i>Wolves</i></a> from the School Library Journal's Top 100 Children's Book List, which is a terrific resource. Its popularity spawned a series, but I don't remember how good the rest are.<br /><br />I read this a ton of times as a kid, and re-reading it now, scenes absolutely exploded in my memory as I got to them. Aunt Julia's pathetic poverty, Simon's hidden cave, Mrs. Brisket's nasty daughter finding and breaking an egg in Bonnie's pocket...This is one of the first books in which I felt real danger. When Bonnie and Sylvia are in jeopardy, they're <i>really</i> in jeopardy. <br /><br />I wasn't wrong when I was young; this is legitimately wonderful. Now that I fully recognize all the tropes Aiken is playing with, it might be even better. It has brave heroines and narrow escapes, and it's about as perfect as children's literature has ever been.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15039296655784070084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_9681676" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9681676" />
    <a title="Mariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/647547-mariel"><img alt="Mariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451321467p2/647547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9681676?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariel" href="/user/show/647547-mariel">Mariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">angels with even filthier souls</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mariel by: </span>
      angels with filthy souls
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9681676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer868603103594026803">The Wolves of Willoughby Chase is best read when young, or by those with the ability to tap into their inner girl.<br/><br/>I enjoyed the evil impostors who gleefully inflict child abuse. 'Wolves' is best read by kids who love to feel a bit of self-pity and delicious horror.<br/>Bonnie is a bit of a simpering thing and there are lots of mentions of dresses and lace. I didn't care about that. My eyes tend to glaze over fripperies in real life too. (It feels like I'm the only person alive who doesn't notice if s</span>
  <span id="freeText868603103594026803" style="display:none">The Wolves of Willoughby Chase is best read when young, or by those with the ability to tap into their inner girl.<br /><br />I enjoyed the evil impostors who gleefully inflict child abuse. 'Wolves' is best read by kids who love to feel a bit of self-pity and delicious horror.<br />Bonnie is a bit of a simpering thing and there are lots of mentions of dresses and lace. I didn't care about that. My eyes tend to glaze over fripperies in real life too. (It feels like I'm the only person alive who doesn't notice if someone mismatches their socks.) Sylvia had more spunk, if she was spoiled. I liked her a lot when she was knocked down some pegs.<br /><br />Wait, I don't know what my inner girl is. I liked the baddies! I rooted for the baddies as a kid. I wanted Ursula to win (don't get me started on my hatred of being called "Ariel" or, even worse, "The Little Mermaid". The 'm' is not silent, little me would rage.) I liked pretty much all the Disney baddies up until the creepy bearded dude from Aladdin. The baddies in 'Wolves' are great. They eat all of the good food for themselves. They send the girls off to an evil boarding school/slave house (Mr. Brocklehurst would die of envy). They sleep in and are bad in a way that Lemony Snickett wouldn't dream of. (Phillip Pullman too ripped off Aiken's series.)<br /><br />There are also cool wolves. Aiken writes atmospheric creepy wolf stuff very well. It's like a dark side of girly books like Avonlea or something. I'm weird or something because I actually found this more cozy than that.<br /><br />The Dido Twite books in the series are pure awesomeness and way, way better than 'Wolves'. I did not know about those until my adulthood, though. I skipped college classes to blow through all of them. Maybe I would have done that anyway. Anyway, they are super. Simon, the boy who lives in a cave, is the hero of Blackhearts in Battersea and Dido Twite appears. The rest of the books are hers because she owns.<br /><br /> If you dig long range cannons, plots to overthrow kings, grinding bones to make your bread, kidnapping and pink whales: read those books.<br /><br />There was a film version made that has very little to do with this book. I saw it on tv when I was in middle school, and remember that I was much confused by the shared title. Where did they get the turning kids into soap stuff from? Sigh.<br /><br />P.s. Edward Gorey did the usa covers. Suck on that, England.</span>
  <a data-text-id="868603103594026803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15784216438061309437" style="display:none">Set in 1832, in an imaginary period of history, where wolves roamed during the snow covered days of winter, Sir Willoughby is preparing to take his wife on a cruise as she is delicate and in need of a rest (raise eyebrows) and their daughter Bonnie is awaiting the arrival of her cousin Sylvia who is to come and live with them. Bonnie's life couldn't be happier with rooms full of toys, a dolls house you can walk inside and devoted servants....until Miss Slighcarp arrives.<br /><br />Miss Slighcarp is a real boo-hiss villain and instantly shows that she is not someone you would leave your child with for one second but Lady Willoughby does need that cruise, so they leave and will not be available for contact until they reach port in several months time (handy).<br /><br />Miss Slighcarp wastes no time in <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ dismissing servants, selling the contents of the house, including horror of horrors toys and dolls, burning wills and arranging an accident with the cruise ship  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> she really is award winning meanie material.<br /><br />The rest of the story is very exciting, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Bonnie and Sylvia get sent to an orphanage and even Sylvia's great Aunt is in danger from these villains, who's greed will stop at nothing <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />A hugely satisfying ending to a really exciting story.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1468637655" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8391855607096829822">★★★★✰ 4 stars <br/><br/><b>The best childhood stories have wolves in them.</b> <br/>Often they are evil and dangerous creatures...and yet, there is something beguiling about them. Perhaps there is a freedom to their unrestrained roaming...the ones in <i>The Wolves of Willoughby Chase </i> are undoubtedly<b> wild and ferocious creatures</b> but they are not the story's villains.<br/><br/><b>The fairy-tale elements and imagery contribute to the novel's simultaneously cozy and spine-tingling atmosphere. </b><br/>Set in an alternative history of early-19th</span>
  <span id="freeText8391855607096829822" style="display:none">★★★★✰ 4 stars <br><br><b>The best childhood stories have wolves in them.</b> <br>Often they are evil and dangerous creatures...and yet, there is something beguiling about them. Perhaps there is a freedom to their unrestrained roaming...the ones in <i>The Wolves of Willoughby Chase </i> are undoubtedly<b> wild and ferocious creatures</b> but they are not the story's villains.<br><br><b>The fairy-tale elements and imagery contribute to the novel's simultaneously cozy and spine-tingling atmosphere. </b><br>Set in an alternative history of early-19th century England, <i> The Wolves of Willoughby Chase </i> follows the adventurous of two cousins as they try to escape from the evil clutches of their new governess and her cronies. We have bold Bonnie, daughter of Sir Willoughby, and her more timid cousin Sylvia who is an orphan and was raised by her frail aunt. When Sir Willoughby takes his wife onto a voyage for her health, he leaves Bonnie and Sylvia at Willoughby Chase. The two girls soon realise that their new governess Miss Slighcarp is up to no good. <b>What follows is an engrossing adventure starring two brave children, train rides across dark forests, wicked governesses and teachers, a horrid boarding 'school', and many dangerous treks across forests teeming with wolves. </b><br><br>Aiken's deceptively simple language ingeniously conjures Bonnie and Sylvia's adventures in a way that reflects their 'young' point of view. The adults have a certain Dickensian quality to them that is apparent through their names and appearances. <br><br><b>There is so much to love in these pages.</b> We have snow, sumptuous meals, hidden passageways, shipwrecks, and daring escapes. In spite of the many injustices Bonnie and Sylvia are made to experience, there is always <b>an undercurrent of hope</b> in this narrative. <br>Perhaps I love this novel so much because<b>it speaks of my childhood</b>, perhaps I simply recognise for what it is.<br><br><a href="https://wishfullyreading.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Read more reviews on my blog</a> / / / <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/9429655-anna-luce" rel="nofollow noopener">View all my reviews on Goodreads</a><br><br>PS: The Folio edition of this novel is gorgeous.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580235509i/28858787._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8391855607096829822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_514186075" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/514186075" />
    <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks"><img alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577577052p2/3533262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/514186075?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey (prettybooks)" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099572879" href="/book/show/15796901-the-wolves-of-willoughby-chase">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=classics-challenge">classics-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer514186075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12574908011426728702"><i>This post is part of the <a href='https://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2015/03/22/the-wolves-of-willoughby-chase-by-joan-aiken-classic-2/' rel='nofollow noopener'>2015 Classics Challenge</a>.</i><br/><br/><strong>WHEN I Discovered This Classic</strong><br/>I actually don't think I had heard of <em>The Wolves of Willoughby Chase</em> until I discovered the <a href='http://www.randomhouse.co.uk/editions/imprint/vintage-childrens-classics' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vintage Children's Classics</a>, my favourite series of children's classics – I just love the design and the selection of well-known and lesser-known classics! I bought <em>I Capture the Castle</em> in 2012 followed by <em>The</em> <em>Wolves of Willoughby Chase</em>, <em>The Dark is Rising</em>, <em>Fly Away Home</em> and <em>Charlotte Sometimes</em> in 2013.<br/><br/><strong>WHY I Chose to Read It </strong><br/>It</span>
  <span id="freeText12574908011426728702" style="display:none"><i>This post is part of the <a href="https://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2015/03/22/the-wolves-of-willoughby-chase-by-joan-aiken-classic-2/" rel="nofollow noopener">2015 Classics Challenge</a>.</i><br /><br /><strong>WHEN I Discovered This Classic</strong><br />I actually don't think I had heard of <em>The Wolves of Willoughby Chase</em> until I discovered the <a href="http://www.randomhouse.co.uk/editions/imprint/vintage-childrens-classics" rel="nofollow noopener">Vintage Children's Classics</a>, my favourite series of children's classics – I just love the design and the selection of well-known and lesser-known classics! I bought <em>I Capture the Castle</em> in 2012 followed by <em>The</em> <em>Wolves of Willoughby Chase</em>, <em>The Dark is Rising</em>, <em>Fly Away Home</em> and <em>Charlotte Sometimes</em> in 2013.<br /><br /><strong>WHY I Chose to Read It </strong><br />It was<em> freezing</em> in February and I was looking for a wintry classic to read as part of the challenge. It had been sitting on my TBR for a while and I hadn't picked up a Vintage Children's Classic for a while, even though I own quite a few now. It's also meant to be adapted as a BBC drama this Christmas, but I have not heard any more about it since it was first announced in 2013. I really hope it goes ahead!<br /><br /><strong>WHAT Makes It A Classic</strong><br />It's a classic children's adventure story, full of beautiful descriptions of the landscape, treacherous characters and a thrilling mystery to solve. It has a bunch of characters – from Bonnie and Sylvia themselves to the adult servants that aid their mission – that you'll be rooting for all the way. A debate arises now and again about how dark children's and young adult literature has become, but you only have to meet Miss Slighcarp and her allies to realise it has always been that way – they're truly ghastly! Although <em>The Wolves of Willoughby Chase</em> is over 50 years old, its themes of friendship, class, gender, and the tendency of adults to underestimate children still resonate today.<br /><br /><strong>WHAT I Thought of This Classic</strong><br />I adored it instantly! I was fascinated by the idea of an alternative Britain where wolves may attack at any time. I expected the story to be more about the wolves, but it's actually about how the wolves aren't the real enemy here. It's wonderfully written and I loved the vivid descriptions of Willoughby Chase, from the stark white landscape to Bonnie's delightful toy room. It has secret passages, charming characters (like Simon the gooseboy) and a story that doesn't patronise children. It has everything you could want. I'm looking forward to reading <em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36637.Black_Hearts_in_Battersea__The_Wolves_Chronicles___2_" title="Black Hearts in Battersea (The Wolves Chronicles, #2) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Hearts at Battersea</a>
</em>, the next book.<br /><br /><strong>WILL It Stay A Classic</strong><br />I think so! It still feels fresh and exciting. I hope the forthcoming BBC drama does the book justice and encourages more people to read this wonderful story. And once you've done that, there's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41915-the-wolves-chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">11 more books in the series</a> for you to read.<br /><br /><strong>WHO I’d Recommend It To</strong><br />People who <strong>l</strong>ove children's books and want to delve into the world of classics. People who love children's adventure and mystery stories, like the Laura Marlin mysteries. People who love how atmospheric Gothic literature can be, like <em>Jane Eyre</em>.<br /><br /><i>I also reviewed this book over on <a href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Books</a>.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12574908011426728702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Willow " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4529669-willow"><img alt="Willow " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472180488p2/4529669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1026950744?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Willow " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Willow " href="/user/show/4529669-willow">Willow </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1026950744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11044821540264850663">The Wolves of Willoughby Chase is a lovely little children’s book with secret passages, an evil governess and a goose boy. I definitely recommend it to little girls who have a mind for adventure. I myself had a little trouble at first getting into it, simply because I’m just not the audience for this. But eventually the adventure took over and I wanted to find out what happens. <br/><br/>There’s a weird wackiness in the beginning, which made me chuckle. Wolves jump up and attack the windows on a train. Bo</span>
  <span id="freeText11044821540264850663" style="display:none">The Wolves of Willoughby Chase is a lovely little children’s book with secret passages, an evil governess and a goose boy. I definitely recommend it to little girls who have a mind for adventure. I myself had a little trouble at first getting into it, simply because I’m just not the audience for this. But eventually the adventure took over and I wanted to find out what happens. <br /><br />There’s a weird wackiness in the beginning, which made me chuckle. Wolves jump up and attack the windows on a train. Bonnie’s parents have no problem leaving their home and their bank accounts to a distant relative who has a very unpleasant disposition. A boy lives in a cave with his geese, even in the winter. And the evil plot---I won’t even go into it. Let’s just say, I seriously have my doubts. It was fun though. :)<br /><br />This is an old story (from 1962) so it has kind of has an old-world charm. There’s not a patronizing message (which most children's stories have today) just a melodrama, and the villains are so obvious, I almost felt like I should boo and hiss when they popped up in the story. Aiken has a lovely way with words and description that made me feel like I had slipped into a fairytale. <br /><br />I give four stars! Thank you Jeanette and Diane Lynn for the fun quick buddy read. :D<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11044821540264850663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margaret" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margaret" href="/user/show/1379840-margaret">Margaret</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1379840-margaret?shelf=childhood-standouts">childhood-standouts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28837204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15527376907314839037">"It was dusk -- winter dusk. Snow lay white and shining over the pleated hills, and icicles hung from the forest trees. Snow lay piled on the dark road across Willoughby Wold, but from dawn men had been clearing it with brooms and shovels. There were hundreds of them at work, wrapped in sacking because of the bitter cold, and keeping together in groups for fear of the wolves, made savage and reckless from hunger..." <br/>I dare you not to go on reading after that. <br/> I read this book over and over as a</span>
  <span id="freeText15527376907314839037" style="display:none">"It was dusk -- winter dusk. Snow lay white and shining over the pleated hills, and icicles hung from the forest trees. Snow lay piled on the dark road across Willoughby Wold, but from dawn men had been clearing it with brooms and shovels. There were hundreds of them at work, wrapped in sacking because of the bitter cold, and keeping together in groups for fear of the wolves, made savage and reckless from hunger..." <br />I dare you not to go on reading after that. <br /> I read this book over and over as a kid, but it's equally entertaining for adults - it's the book Dickens might have written if he wrote for young people, an atmospheric semi-Gothic that follows the adventures of two young girls, spunky intrepid Bonnie and her fragile cousin Sylvia, when Bonnie's parents go abroad and leave them with the malign governess Miss Slighcarp, who is definitely up to no good. Joan Aiken is the daughter of poet Conrad Aiken, and her heritage shows in her vivid use of language, but it's really the great characters that make this one so memorable: dauntless heroines, some truly repugnant villains, and in Simon the clever goose-boy and Pattern the faithful housemaid the kind of loyal and fearless friends we all hope to find, and sometimes are lucky enough to. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15527376907314839037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_27583056" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27583056" />
    <a title="W.B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/545392-w-b"><img alt="W.B." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373322692p2/545392.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27583056?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="W.B." class="user" itemprop="url" name="W.B." href="/user/show/545392-w-b">W.B.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27583056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5826080029430540914">This is terrible but wonderful.<br/><br/>It's really a book that was published for young adults or kids, but published in 1962 so the idea of what constitutes entertaining literature for youngsters is really rather dated.<br/><br/>I think the author was more influenced by Edward Gorey and his odd, brilliant little books than she was by some of the other palpable influences, like Dickens and other masters of "waif literature."<br/><br/>It's the story of a rich little "waif" (so not a true waif, but she fits the archetypal mol</span>
  <span id="freeText5826080029430540914" style="display:none">This is terrible but wonderful.<br /><br />It's really a book that was published for young adults or kids, but published in 1962 so the idea of what constitutes entertaining literature for youngsters is really rather dated.<br /><br />I think the author was more influenced by Edward Gorey and his odd, brilliant little books than she was by some of the other palpable influences, like Dickens and other masters of "waif literature."<br /><br />It's the story of a rich little "waif" (so not a true waif, but she fits the archetypal mold) who is left under the guardianship of a questionable governess, Miss Slighcarp, who arrives at the familial estate (Willoughby Chase)under questionable circumstances to begin her reign of terror over children.<br /><br />So very Gorey.<br /><br />Even the cover art (and many of the illustrations throughout) are a total Gorey rip-off.<br /><br />I researched it to make sure it wasn't one of Gorey's many pseudonyms, but this seems to just be a case of an epigonus.<br /><br />Most likely, the author or someone responsible for the book design urged the illustrator in that direction.<br /><br />The book is ridiculous but fun. <br /><br />The author has such a strange lexicon, and writes in purple prose, which is actually what makes the book fun. <br /><br />It's a bon-bon. Nothing more.<br /><br />But bon-bons can be fun. Let your mind get fat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5826080029430540914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=key-stage-2">key-stage-2</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=absence-of-parents">absence-of-parents</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1401696665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5085591332784393274">I'm still in two minds about this book. I enjoyed it very much, this was the first Aiken I have read and realise that I should have read far more since she's such an established and well-received children's author. The first half of the novel, set in Willoughby Hall is wonderful. The story is set in an alternate Victorian England. This is an England hoarded with wolves that have migrated through mainland Europe from Russia through a pre-Eurotunnel undersea excavation. <br/>The story reads like a Dick</span>
  <span id="freeText5085591332784393274" style="display:none">I'm still in two minds about this book. I enjoyed it very much, this was the first Aiken I have read and realise that I should have read far more since she's such an established and well-received children's author. The first half of the novel, set in Willoughby Hall is wonderful. The story is set in an alternate Victorian England. This is an England hoarded with wolves that have migrated through mainland Europe from Russia through a pre-Eurotunnel undersea excavation. <br />The story reads like a Dickensian classic filled with wonderful characters, as good or as evil as you can get. The story is gripping and, rarely for me, there were points where I wasn't sure what would happen to the protagonists. The antagonists themselves may seem Dahl-esque in their appearance but they're far better in their craft and more like Dickens' work. <br />Yet, I wanted more wolves. They are there, always, as a dark and unsettling threat for the first half of the story and then, when we move to London, they are missing. For me, it was this dark and constantly looming danger that set this story apart and I wished Aiken had stayed with it more. Nevertheless, this is a great read indeed for any KS2 class. The language is rich and stylistically very unique: a pleasure to read once you're comfortable with it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5085591332784393274" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_83881635" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83881635" />
    <a title="Margaret" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/162759-margaret"><img alt="Margaret" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1234732285p2/162759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83881635?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margaret" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margaret" href="/user/show/162759-margaret">Margaret</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440996293" href="/book/show/1311537.The_Wolves_of_Willoughby_Chase">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=2019-read">2019-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=authors-ab">authors-ab</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=fantasy-and-science-fiction">fantasy-and-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=children-s-and-ya-fiction">children-s-and-ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162759-margaret?shelf=2005-read">2005-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83881635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2981147432701058526">Joan Aiken's Wolves Chronicles are wildly inventive fantasies, set in an alternate England where the Stuarts remained on the throne, making the Hanoverians the rebels and conspirators, and where wolves still roam even in London. There are eleven of them in all (and won't be any more, since Aiken sadly died in January 2004), and I think of them in sets of two or three.<br/><br/><i>The Wolves of Willoughby Chase</i> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36637.Black_Hearts_in_Battersea__The_Wolves_Chronicles___2_' title='Black Hearts in Battersea (The Wolves Chronicles, #2) by Joan Aiken' rel='nofollow noopener'>Black Hearts in Battersea</a> introduce many of the main characters in the series, chiefly Simon, a</span>
  <span id="freeText2981147432701058526" style="display:none">Joan Aiken's Wolves Chronicles are wildly inventive fantasies, set in an alternate England where the Stuarts remained on the throne, making the Hanoverians the rebels and conspirators, and where wolves still roam even in London. There are eleven of them in all (and won't be any more, since Aiken sadly died in January 2004), and I think of them in sets of two or three.<br /><br /><i>The Wolves of Willoughby Chase</i> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36637.Black_Hearts_in_Battersea__The_Wolves_Chronicles___2_" title="Black Hearts in Battersea (The Wolves Chronicles, #2) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Hearts in Battersea</a> introduce many of the main characters in the series, chiefly Simon, an orphan, and Dido Twite, a London guttersnipe, as well as Dido's family, inveterate Hanoverian plotters, especially her Pa, a musical but amoral genius. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36644.Nightbirds_on_Nantucket__The_Wolves_Chronicles___3_" title="Nightbirds on Nantucket (The Wolves Chronicles, #3) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Nightbirds on Nantucket</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36635.The_Stolen_Lake__The_Wolves_Chronicles___4_" title="The Stolen Lake (The Wolves Chronicles, #4) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stolen Lake</a> chronicle Dido's adventures outside England (as does <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/74045.Dangerous_Games__Riley_Jenson_Guardian__4_" title="Dangerous Games (Riley Jenson Guardian #4) by Keri Arthur" rel="nofollow noopener">Dangerous Games</a>, though it was written after Dido and Pa), and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36641.The_Cuckoo_Tree__The_Wolves_Chronicles___6_" title="The Cuckoo Tree (The Wolves Chronicles, #6) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cuckoo Tree</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/916666.Dido_and_Pa__The_Wolves_Chronicles___7_" title="Dido and Pa (The Wolves Chronicles, #7) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Dido and Pa</a> tell what happens when she returns. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17876.Notes_from_Underground__White_Nights__The_Dream_of_a_Ridiculous_Man__and_Selections_from_The_House_of_the_Dead" title="Notes from Underground, White Nights, The Dream of a Ridiculous Man, and Selections from The House of the Dead by Fyodor Dostoyevsky" rel="nofollow noopener">Is Underground</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/292661.Cold_Shoulder_Road__The_Wolves_Chronicles___9_" title="Cold Shoulder Road (The Wolves Chronicles, #9) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Cold Shoulder Road</a> tell of Dido's sister Is, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/262741.Midwinter_Nightingale__The_Wolves_Chronicles___10_" title="Midwinter Nightingale (The Wolves Chronicles, #10) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Midwinter Nightingale</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/751560.The_Witch_of_Clatteringshaws__The_Wolves_Chronicles___11_" title="The Witch of Clatteringshaws (The Wolves Chronicles, #11) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Witch of Clatteringshaws</a> return to Dido and Simon's stories.<br /><br />Most people seem to think that the first three books are the best, and I'd agree with that; they have more focused plots than some of the later books. I do have an odd fondness for <i>The Stolen Lake</i>, which has Dido encountering ancient Britons in South America and an interesting Arthurian plot, but by <i>Dido and Pa</i>, I am generally happy to get back to England and Aiken's exploration of Dido's relationship with her family. Although the two Is books are very good, though significantly bleaker than the rest of the series (and Aiken is never afraid to be bleak or frightening), I was disappointed with the last two books, which are weaker of plot than the earlier ones. However, all of them are worth reading, and the first three are generally considered classics of children's fantasy; once you've read those, you'll want to read all eleven of them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2981147432701058526" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_19480342" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19480342" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/218078-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541280315p2/218078.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19480342?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/218078-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/218078-danielle?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/218078-danielle?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/218078-danielle?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19480342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer685114823417986785">I read this book thinking, "I wish this had been around when I was younger..." Well, this is a foolish thought because the books were around when I was a child, and have been around for awhile. <br/>Any books for children that feature a mixture of Georgian/Victorian society, a dash of wolves, loads of adventure, and little girls learning to stand on their own two solid feet has my love. I love that Bonnie is not only a plucky young girl, but also handy with a rifle (good against wolves!). <br/>This story </span>
  <span id="freeText685114823417986785" style="display:none">I read this book thinking, "I wish this had been around when I was younger..." Well, this is a foolish thought because the books were around when I was a child, and have been around for awhile. <br />Any books for children that feature a mixture of Georgian/Victorian society, a dash of wolves, loads of adventure, and little girls learning to stand on their own two solid feet has my love. I love that Bonnie is not only a plucky young girl, but also handy with a rifle (good against wolves!). <br />This story is one of daring, bravery, friendship, sisterhood and that very best ingredient in children's stories -- growing up with grace away from parents and adults. <br /><br />I do wish I'd read this book as a young girl because I could have learned and gained a great deal from Bonnie even if I was more like shy, sensitive Sylvia at first. This book is recommended to young girls (and boys) and any adult that still enjoys that bit of whimsy and wonder in their reading. I would think this would be a great read-aloud and share book.<br /><br />ps. See the Strange Horizons review of more of Joan Aiken's book for a more clear picture of this Wolves series. <a href="http://www.strangehorizons.com/2001/20011029/wolves.shtml" rel="nofollow noopener">Find the review here.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="685114823417986785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103575356" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103575356" />
    <a title="Leslie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/845910-leslie"><img alt="Leslie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1201621360p2/845910.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103575356?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslie" href="/user/show/845910-leslie">Leslie</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer103575356&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103575356" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5184262391467123702">In this tome, cousins Sylvia (poor meek city mouse) and Bonnie (rich haughty country mouse) reunite and band together against wolves and vile spinster governesses (or as one servant says: HARRIDANS!)while their guardians are on sea voyage. <br/><br/>This is a decent book, but my overwhelming feeling (and this is a rare one!) is that it ought to have been at least 100 pages longer. There are several ends that Aiken leaves untied. The most criminal loose end is the "wolf pack without" with all of their supe</span>
  <span id="freeText5184262391467123702" style="display:none">In this tome, cousins Sylvia (poor meek city mouse) and Bonnie (rich haughty country mouse) reunite and band together against wolves and vile spinster governesses (or as one servant says: HARRIDANS!)while their guardians are on sea voyage. <br /><br />This is a decent book, but my overwhelming feeling (and this is a rare one!) is that it ought to have been at least 100 pages longer. There are several ends that Aiken leaves untied. The most criminal loose end is the "wolf pack without" with all of their supernatural potential; they fade out midway through without so much as a shape-shift or a green eye aglow. Why is the manor hounded by perilous wolves? Beats me! Similarly, I was so on board when the girls arrive at the corrupt orphanage. There they relinquish their names for numerals (98 and 99 respectively) and exchange the trimmings/finery of Victorian girlhood (petticoats! plaits! pelisses!) for cropped haircuts and coveralls. I only wish they'd lingered there longer; I like to roll about and laze in my depravity, thank you!<br /><br />One very interesting aspect, as this is a book for children, is the meditation on class/gender. The girls come from distinct class backgrounds, each with their own codes for what it means to be a noble little lady-to-be. The servants are dutiful on the whole, timidly risking their jobs to help the girls as they can. Perhaps the most intriguing character is Simon, a foundling goose-boy who once suffered at the hand of a cruel master. He steals away to live off the land, raising fowl and dining on chestnuts to get by. His quarters are described favorably as "snug" and "clean." When the girls escape the orphanage, it is through Simon's wile; under his wing they grow robust and hearty. When Bonnie's parents return from sea, her mother comments that she suffered "shocks and privations" under the care of the "savages" who rescued her, but that to her surprise her health improved. When Bonnie has the opportunity to trade her suit for a gown, she remarks that she's "grown accustomed to boy's clothes." Each character comes away less moored to convention.<br /><br />This reminded me a lot of Angela Carter's The Magic Toyshop, a decidedly darker, more racy contemporary take on Victorian girlhood and what it means to be an orphan.<br /><br />Let's watch the movie!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5184262391467123702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1389233539" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1389233539" />
    <a title="Pam Baddeley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42764850-pam-baddeley"><img alt="Pam Baddeley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442488147p2/42764850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1389233539?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pam Baddeley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pam Baddeley" href="/user/show/42764850-pam-baddeley">Pam Baddeley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140303100" href="/book/show/1955124.The_Wolves_of_Willoughby_Chase">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42764850-pam-baddeley?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42764850-pam-baddeley?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42764850-pam-baddeley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1389233539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8362847780768670055">I approached this book with a little apprehension as I have had past experience of re-reading old childhood favourites and feeling letdown, but there was no problem with this novel, set in an alternative 1832 where the monarch is James III (implying that the House of Hanover never came to the throne) and wolves have entered England during a bad winter by crossing the Channel Tunnel (not opened in our reality until 1994).<br/><br/>Unlike the children's books of today - this was first published in the early</span>
  <span id="freeText8362847780768670055" style="display:none">I approached this book with a little apprehension as I have had past experience of re-reading old childhood favourites and feeling letdown, but there was no problem with this novel, set in an alternative 1832 where the monarch is James III (implying that the House of Hanover never came to the throne) and wolves have entered England during a bad winter by crossing the Channel Tunnel (not opened in our reality until 1994).<br /><br />Unlike the children's books of today - this was first published in the early 1960s - the whole thing proceeds at a riproaring pace with very little build-up. We plunge straight into the situation: the wealthy parents of Bonnie are about to embark on a trip abroad for the mother's health, and a governess, Miss Slighcarp, who is also a distant relation, has been hired to run the estate and teach Bonnie and her cousin, Sylvia. Meanwhile, Sylvia, raised by the impoverished sister of Bonnie's father, who is too proud to admit her situation, is put aboard a train to travel to the country estate. A seemingly jovial man travels in the same compartment and makes himself useful when the train is attacked by wolves, but soon after arrival, both he and the governess show their true colours and the adventure is underway, incorporating boys who live in the woods, geese, a Dickensian orphange and a shipwreck, among other elements.<br /><br />The story is told in bold strokes with melodrama, larger than life villains, faithful retainers who are indispensible to the children's safety, and parents or guardians who are conveniently got out of the way by various mechanisms. The only slight detraction is that the wolves of the title fade away by the time the weather warms, and the book does not feature Dido Twite, who I recall as being the streetwise heroine of Aiken's alternative 19th century tales, but who is not introduced until <i>Black Hearts in Battersea</i>. But otherwise an engaging and speedy read which earns 4 stars from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8362847780768670055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1389233539">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1738709-lethe?shelf=a-children">a-children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1738709-lethe?shelf=g-fantasy">g-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2193622022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11156533190286059921">After a promising (but strangely familiar) start, this turned into a caricature, with over-the-top evil villains and a saccharine happy ending in which everything was tied up neatly in a bow.<br/><br/>I read in the "Backstory" that Aiken had originally written it as a one-off spoof of the Victorian gothic adventure stories she had read as a child. As far as I'm concerned, it didn't work. The parody will fly over children's heads and the story is way too simplistic and sugary sweet for adults.<br/><br/>In my opinion</span>
  <span id="freeText11156533190286059921" style="display:none">After a promising (but strangely familiar) start, this turned into a caricature, with over-the-top evil villains and a saccharine happy ending in which everything was tied up neatly in a bow.<br /><br />I read in the "Backstory" that Aiken had originally written it as a one-off spoof of the Victorian gothic adventure stories she had read as a child. As far as I'm concerned, it didn't work. The parody will fly over children's heads and the story is way too simplistic and sugary sweet for adults.<br /><br />In my opinion, the best part of the book is the cover illustration, by Rohan Eason.</span>

<div id="review_2578609054" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2578609054" />
    <a title="Abigail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail"><img alt="Abigail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539121384p2/87835420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2578609054?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abigail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abigail" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail">Abigail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/19051897-the-wolves-of-willoughby-chase">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Young Readers Who Enjoy Gothic Adventure Fiction</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fantasy">childrens-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=governesses">governesses</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2578609054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17651702571578016759">Cousins Bonnie and Sylvia Green find themselves in danger when Bonnie's parents must leave the country, entrusting the girls to the care of their wicked governess, Miss Slighcarp. But whether they are confronting the eponymous wolves of Willoughby Chase or enduring the drudgery of a charity school, our two young heroines never lose sight of their goal: to expose the machinations of their enemy, and regain their home...<br/><br/>The first in what is sometimes called the <i>Wolves Chronicles</i>, a loosely-connect</span>
  <span id="freeText17651702571578016759" style="display:none">Cousins Bonnie and Sylvia Green find themselves in danger when Bonnie's parents must leave the country, entrusting the girls to the care of their wicked governess, Miss Slighcarp. But whether they are confronting the eponymous wolves of Willoughby Chase or enduring the drudgery of a charity school, our two young heroines never lose sight of their goal: to expose the machinations of their enemy, and regain their home...<br /><br />The first in what is sometimes called the <i>Wolves Chronicles</i>, a loosely-connected series of children's books, mainly considered fantasy because they occur in an alternate nineteenth-century England. In this alternative time-line, the Hanoverian line never comes to power in England, and the country has remained largely undeveloped, despite the advent of the Industrial Revolution.<br /><br />This tongue-in-cheek Victorian melodrama, packed with non-stop action and adventure, set the standard for many children's books to follow, not the least of which is <i>A Series of Unfortunate Events</i> by Lemony Snicket. An exciting and entertaining read on its own, it also introduces the character of Simon the goose-boy, who will play such a large part in the books to come...<br /><br />While the cover illustrations by Edward Gorey are justly beloved, this book would not be the same without Pat Marriott's interior illustrations.<br /><br /><br /><b>Addendum</b>: Because the reading order of this series is somewhat complicated, I have included this handy guide, which is organized by publication date, and which I recommend to prospective readers of the series, rather than the one offered here on Goodreads:<br /><br />Reading Order for the Series:<br /><br />1) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36638.The_Wolves_of_Willoughby_Chase__The_Wolves_Chronicles___1_" title="The Wolves of Willoughby Chase (The Wolves Chronicles, #1) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wolves of Willoughby Chase</a><br /><br />2) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36637.Black_Hearts_in_Battersea__The_Wolves_Chronicles___2_" title="Black Hearts in Battersea (The Wolves Chronicles, #2) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Hearts in Battersea</a><br /><br />3) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36644.Nightbirds_on_Nantucket__The_Wolves_Chronicles___3_" title="Nightbirds on Nantucket (The Wolves Chronicles, #3) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Nightbirds on Nantucket</a><br /><br />4) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/262742.The_Whispering_Mountain__The_Wolves_Chronicles___0_" title="The Whispering Mountain (The Wolves Chronicles, #0) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Whispering Mountain</a><br /><br />5) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36641.The_Cuckoo_Tree__The_Wolves_Chronicles___6_" title="The Cuckoo Tree (The Wolves Chronicles, #6) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cuckoo Tree</a><br /><br />6) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36635.The_Stolen_Lake__The_Wolves_Chronicles___4_" title="The Stolen Lake (The Wolves Chronicles, #4) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stolen Lake</a><br /><br />7) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/916666.Dido_and_Pa__The_Wolves_Chronicles___7_" title="Dido and Pa (The Wolves Chronicles, #7) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Dido and Pa</a><br /><br />8) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/292660.Is_Underground__The_Wolves_Chronicles___8_" title="Is Underground (The Wolves Chronicles, #8) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Is Underground</a><br /><br />9) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/292661.Cold_Shoulder_Road__The_Wolves_Chronicles___9_" title="Cold Shoulder Road (The Wolves Chronicles, #9) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Cold Shoulder Road</a><br /><br />10) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36642.Dangerous_Games__The_Wolves_Chronicles___5_" title="Dangerous Games (The Wolves Chronicles, #5) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Dangerous Games</a><br /><br />11) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/262741.Midwinter_Nightingale__The_Wolves_Chronicles___10_" title="Midwinter Nightingale (The Wolves Chronicles, #10) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Midwinter Nightingale</a><br /><br />12) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/751560.The_Witch_of_Clatteringshaws__The_Wolves_Chronicles___11_" title="The Witch of Clatteringshaws (The Wolves Chronicles, #11) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Witch of Clatteringshaws</a><br /><br />A few notes:<br /><br />--<u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/292660.Is_Underground__The_Wolves_Chronicles___8_" title="Is Underground (The Wolves Chronicles, #8) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Is Underground</a>
</u> is the American name for the British original, <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1311539.Is__The_Wolves_Chronicles___8_" title="Is (The Wolves Chronicles, #8) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Is</a>
</u>. Similarly, <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36642.Dangerous_Games__The_Wolves_Chronicles___5_" title="Dangerous Games (The Wolves Chronicles, #5) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Dangerous Games</a>
</u> was originally published in Britain as <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1155088.Limbo_Lodge__The_Wolves_Chronicles___5_" title="Limbo Lodge (The Wolves Chronicles, #5) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Limbo Lodge</a>
</u>.<br /><br />--<u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36638.The_Wolves_of_Willoughby_Chase__The_Wolves_Chronicles___1_" title="The Wolves of Willoughby Chase (The Wolves Chronicles, #1) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wolves of Willoughby Chase</a>
</u> features two characters that recur, but the two young heroines do not.<br /><br />--<u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36635.The_Stolen_Lake__The_Wolves_Chronicles___4_" title="The Stolen Lake (The Wolves Chronicles, #4) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stolen Lake</a>
</u> is the point at which the chronology becomes somewhat complicated, as it is the sixth book, but chronicles events that occur in between <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1155086.Night_Birds_on_Nantucket__The_Wolves_Chronicles___3_" title="Night Birds on Nantucket (The Wolves Chronicles, #3) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Birds on Nantucket</a>
</u> (#3) and <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36641.The_Cuckoo_Tree__The_Wolves_Chronicles___6_" title="The Cuckoo Tree (The Wolves Chronicles, #6) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cuckoo Tree</a>
</u> (#5).<br /><br />--<u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/292660.Is_Underground__The_Wolves_Chronicles___8_" title="Is Underground (The Wolves Chronicles, #8) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Is Underground</a>
</u> (or <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1311539.Is__The_Wolves_Chronicles___8_" title="Is (The Wolves Chronicles, #8) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Is</a>
</u>) and <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/292661.Cold_Shoulder_Road__The_Wolves_Chronicles___9_" title="Cold Shoulder Road (The Wolves Chronicles, #9) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Cold Shoulder Road</a>
</u> both feature Is Twite, cousin to the main heroine, Dido. They occur alongside the other books, and their position in the series is not chronologically relevant.<br /><br />--<u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36642.Dangerous_Games__The_Wolves_Chronicles___5_" title="Dangerous Games (The Wolves Chronicles, #5) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Dangerous Games</a>
</u> (<u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1155088.Limbo_Lodge__The_Wolves_Chronicles___5_" title="Limbo Lodge (The Wolves Chronicles, #5) by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Limbo Lodge</a>
</u>) is another title that backtracks in the chronology...<br /><br />--Although not technically part of the series, Aiken's <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36636.Midnight_Is_a_Place" title="Midnight Is a Place by Joan Aiken" rel="nofollow noopener">Midnight Is a Place</a>
</u> does occur in the same alternative timeline, and is set in Blastburn, the same imaginary city that features in the other books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17651702571578016759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The influence of Charles Dickens, Sheridan leFanu, Wilkie Collins, and the Sensation novelists of that time can be seen here. Lots of action and adventure, featuring two brave little girls who save the day. A fun read for all ages.</span>

<div id="review_3212383491" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3212383491" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590863781p2/3498889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3212383491?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/19051897-the-wolves-of-willoughby-chase">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3212383491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18243089274167547789">When I was a child I read this several times, but I haven't since. Naturally, I was concerned it wouldn't hold up. Well, it's Joan Aiken, so I shouldn't have worried... there's so much more here than I remembered. I mostly enjoyed it for the melodrama back then... I empathized so strongly with the children that I almost forgot how happy my real-life family was. Now I realize that it's more like a loving riff on Dickensian themes.<br/><br/>The edition I read from my local library now is original, and has i</span>
  <span id="freeText18243089274167547789" style="display:none">When I was a child I read this several times, but I haven't since. Naturally, I was concerned it wouldn't hold up. Well, it's Joan Aiken, so I shouldn't have worried... there's so much more here than I remembered. I mostly enjoyed it for the melodrama back then... I empathized so strongly with the children that I almost forgot how happy my real-life family was. Now I realize that it's more like a loving riff on Dickensian themes.<br /><br />The edition I read from my local library now is original, and has interesting blurbs on the back. Particularly: <br /><br />"It's a funny book. The language is so fantastically light... It ought to have a double appeal--to readers of 'The Secret Garden' who will take it pretty seriously, and to the more sophisticated readers who, like adults, will find it laughing-out-loud funny."<br /><br />Unpick that if you will!<br /><br />Also, read the book.<br />If you find an edition with illustrations by Pat Marriott, they're pretty cool. A bit like Edward Ardizonne.<br /><br />Btw, the wolves are fairy-tale wolves. Don't worry about children thinking that real wolves will hunt people to the extent that little girls will need to carry fowling pieces or anything.... The excuse given in the book is that they are just very hungry (probably because too many English people are eating all the game).</span>
  <a data-text-id="18243089274167547789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Susan in NC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/883451-susan-in-nc"><img alt="Susan in NC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604597549p2/883451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2511079030?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan in NC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan in NC" href="/user/show/883451-susan-in-nc">Susan in NC</a>
